  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5ac26a68-11f1-41f1-b065-f6a034334917'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText2450126820345421387" style="display:none"><i>There is an alternate cover edition for this ASIN <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34857305-paper-princess" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</i><br /><br />From strip clubs and truck stops to southern coast mansions and prep schools, one girl tries to stay true to herself.<br /><br />These Royals will ruin you…<br /><br />Ella Harper is a survivor—a pragmatic optimist. She’s spent her whole life moving from town to town with her flighty mother, struggling to make ends meet and believing that someday she’ll climb out of the gutter. After her mother’s death, Ella is truly alone. <br /><br />Until Callum Royal appears, plucking Ella out of poverty and tossing her into his posh mansion among his five sons who all hate her. Each Royal boy is more magnetic than the last, but none as captivating as Reed Royal, the boy who is determined to send her back to the slums she came from.<br /><br />Reed doesn’t want her. He says she doesn’t belong with the Royals.<br /><br />He might be right.<br /><br />Wealth. Excess. Deception. It’s like nothing Ella has ever experienced, and if she’s going to survive her time in the Royal palace, she’ll need to learn to issue her own Royal decrees. </span>

<div id="review_1773172451" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1773172451" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1773172451?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1773172451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1027476694625411214">Are you ready for a rant? BECAUSE I AM SUPER MAD RIGHT NOW. <b>This book is disgustingly problematic, sexist, and abusive.</b> I actually had no idea what I was in for....I liked the title, okay?! But I read in someone else's review that "Erin Watt" is a pseudonym for two erotica authors. SO. That tells you a lot right there. (Although I'm not 100% sure if it's true or not.)<br/><br/><b>Here is a lovely list of what this book includes:</b><br/>• male dominance and chauvinism and sexism that is NOT rebuffed or called out<br/>• se</span>
  <span id="freeText1027476694625411214" style="display:none">Are you ready for a rant? BECAUSE I AM SUPER MAD RIGHT NOW. <b>This book is disgustingly problematic, sexist, and abusive.</b> I actually had no idea what I was in for....I liked the title, okay?! But I read in someone else's review that "Erin Watt" is a pseudonym for two erotica authors. SO. That tells you a lot right there. (Although I'm not 100% sure if it's true or not.)<br /><br /><b>Here is a lovely list of what this book includes:</b><br />• male dominance and chauvinism and sexism that is NOT rebuffed or called out<br />• sexual harassment and near-rape<br />• romanticising abuse<br />• detailed sex scenes<br />• no plot whatsoever because who needs that<br />• a protagonist who has as much personality as paper (SEE WHAT I DID THERE)<br />• alcohol addiction that is totally shrugged off<br />• DID. I. MENTION. ABUSE. AND. HARASSMENT. YET.<br /><br />I refuse to believe that this kind of story is even remotely okay. I'm not even sure it's YA. The characters are in their teens/highschool but it reads more like New Adult. But the entire romantic plot is <b>an aggressive, rude, domineering, cruel boy and a quiet, passive, innocent, sweet girl have a romance.</b> It's cliche? It's tedious? It's not right.<br /><br /><b>Ella is living with the Royals because their father is her guardian.</b> Like so she's had a bad life, has been a stripper just to make ends meet, blah blah (BUT SHE IS AN INNOCENT PURE OF HEART VIRGIN) and she <i>immediately</i> falls for "bad boy" Reed. Dude. Reed is a disgusting animal. He's rude to Ella from the first time he meets her. He's calling her a slut, talking with his brothers about how it's not safe to have sex with her because she's diseased, he's making sure all the people at school hate her, he treats ALL WOMEN like they're pieces of furniture to use, he <i>walks into her room without knocking</i> while she's changing, and he commands her to go here, stay there, come, sit. WHATEVER. And she just does it because "she can't resist". <b>WHAT PART OF THAT IS OKAY???</b> And then it's just like snap-your-fingers-and-suddenly-he-confesses-he's-only-been-an-evil-jerk-because-he-loves-her.<br /><br />No.<br /><br />Also: no.<br /><br /><b>Here are some delightful examples of how horrendous this romance is:</b><br /><blockquote>They go back to ignoring me. Easton is now telling his brother about the blowjob he got tonight.<br />"It's like she's only giving forty percent now," he gripes. "Used to be a solid hundred, y'know? Going to town on my dick like it's made of chocolate, and suddenly it's a few licks and then <i>let's cuddle</i>? Eff that."<br />Reed snickers. "She thinks she's your girlfriend. Girlfriends don't need to put in an effort."<br />"Yeah, might be time to cut that one loose."</blockquote><br />Wow. When is the time that I'm, like, supposed to think that Reed is a good guy?<br /><blockquote>"I told you to stay away from my brothers," Reed growls. <br />"I'm not a good listener." I start to sit up and then clasp the bedsheets against my chest. I forgot I took my dress off and all I'm wearing are panties.<br />"Sex is sex," he replies darkly. "If I have to fuck you so you don't ruin my family, I'll do it."</blockquote><br /><br />So (A) wtf, (B) how does that makes sense, and (C) the "love interest" is saying he will SEXUALLY ASSULT Ella. And like, the next chapter she feels bad for him because <i>he's just damaged</i> and she apologises for "poking the tiger" because <i>it's all her fault</i>.<br /><br />Do I puke or murder someone?? I'm debating.<br /><br /><blockquote>I drop my arms and walk into the cabin. Something about this guy...he issues a command and I obey. I fight it at first, sure. I always fight, but he always wins.</blockquote><br />And this right here ^^ is an abusive relationship.<br /><br /><b>And that's like the BEGINNING of the problematic issues.</b> The Royal father, Callum, is openly HATED and DESPISED by his five sons. They are disgustingly disrespectful to him. And they're all filthy rich of course, so he just gives them thousands of dollars and then they spit in his face for 100% of the book. <b>Plus they're all drinking, partying, doing drugs, and having sex RIGHT UNDER HIS NOSE.</b> And I can't believe he's oblivious. He's a <i>horrible</i> parent. And not only that but he CONSTANTLY tells Ella what to do. Like "you're going shopping" or "you're going on this boating trip with the family" or "you're going to this party with the boys". Like it's 100% male dominance here too. He doesn't take no for an answer. And everything he does for Ella is "good" in the sense that he's looking out for her. BUT HE 100% DOES NOT RESPECT HER OR HER WISHES. And this is the <i>guardian</i> we're talking about????<br /><br />He also gives Ella 10K per month to stay with his family. I can't even.<br /><br /><b>Like I said: NO PLOT.</b> Perhaps if you got a microscope you might see a <i>very small speck of one.</i> But good luck in that endeavour, fren.<br /><br />It's all just Ella trying to survive the cruelty of highschool and the aggressive harassment of all 5 Royal brothers and then eventually having sex with one for, like, the rest of the book.<br /><br />AND I CAN'T EVEN ROOT FOR ELLA BECAUSE SHE NEVER STANDS UP FOR HERSELF.<br /><br /><b>This isn't romance, it's actually abuse.</b> <br /><br /><b>Not to mention the formatting was really shoddy.</b> Like in the first chapter the font was like changing?? And I don't think it was for aesthetic, because paragraph formatting was also messed up. Also the book was really heavy...like it wasn't printed on normal book paper???<br /><br /><b>ALL IN ALL: look, no. Just no.</b> I'm the one standing in the middle of the room screaming right now because this book was so far in the "THIS IS WRONG" category. It is so sexist and the romance is disgusting and abusive and there is NO WAY you should EVER BE AROUND boys who treat you like you're an object. Reed constantly pins Ella down so she can't leave a situation = THAT'S HARASSMENT AND IT'S ILLEGAL AND REED BELONGS IN PRISON.<br /><br />Either I'm setting fire to this book or my brain to try and forget I read it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1027476694625411214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1576824821" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1576824821" />
    <a title="Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8524618-angie---angie-s-dreamy-reads"><img alt="Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578074503p2/8524618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1576824821?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads" href="/user/show/8524618-angie---angie-s-dreamy-reads">Angie - Angie&#39;s Dreamy Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1576824821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9283827440089656331"><b>WELL THAT WAS A JAW DROPPER!!!!! </b><br/><br/>A fucking <b>JAW DROPPER!!!</b> I'm still reeling! Ahhhhh! Okay... I think I've found a <b>NEW</b> addiction and it's <b>
  <u>ROYALLY</u>
</b> intoxicating!!!! YOU GUYS! I started Paper Princess around 11pm on a Sunday Night. My plan was to read until 12:30. Yeah, <i>rightttttt!!! </i><br/><br/><b>BIGGEST MISTAKE EVER. </b><br/><br/>I had to forced myself to set it down. I had read and read and read and before I knew it I had to be up in 2hrs. TWO HOURS. The next morning I couldn't think. Not about <b>ANYTHING</b> but this book. </span>
  <span id="freeText9283827440089656331" style="display:none"><b>WELL THAT WAS A JAW DROPPER!!!!! </b><br /><br />A fucking <b>JAW DROPPER!!!</b> I'm still reeling! Ahhhhh! Okay... I think I've found a <b>NEW</b> addiction and it's <b>
  <u>ROYALLY</u>
</b> intoxicating!!!! YOU GUYS! I started Paper Princess around 11pm on a Sunday Night. My plan was to read until 12:30. Yeah, <i>rightttttt!!! </i><br /><br /><b>BIGGEST MISTAKE EVER. </b><br /><br />I had to forced myself to set it down. I had read and read and read and before I knew it I had to be up in 2hrs. TWO HOURS. The next morning I couldn't think. Not about <b>ANYTHING</b> but this book. I was obsessed. Intoxicated. Completely taken by what I was reading. As I was making my kids breakfast, my mind ran a marathon, covering every little detail and scene my mind had soaked in. I couldn't get my kids to school fast enough. I came home. I finished immediately. And <b>OH MY WORD!</b> Seriously!!!! <b>THIS</b>, friends, is your <b>NEXT</b> addiction. These Royal's are delightfully wicked in every single way. <br /><br />When you first meet Callum Royal and his sons, you don't know what to think of them. Callum swoops in and saves the day. Literally. I, personally, thought the man was fantastic. Even with his blatant flaws glaring at you, I saw a diamond in the rough. I have a major crush on him. He's HAWT. But his boys... Oh, baby! His five sons left something to be desired. To be honest, at first they're a bunch of assholes. Gorgeous assholes, but fuckers I wanted to throat punch nonetheless. However, first appearances are often times deceiving. There's soooo many things going on in this story. So many skeletons and little hidden compartments lingering behind the scenes, just waiting to jump out. I'm still trying to figure each of them out. <br /><br />One of best things about <i>Paper Princess</i>, my most favorite thing, is Ella herself. Our main character is down right <b>FABULOUS</b>. At 17, this girl has handled more than anyone should. And it hasn't broken her. No, if anything it's made her one hell of a fighter. I respected her. I admired her. She's lost her mother, her father, and she's had to do things, to get by, that made my heart ache. This feisty, yet sweet girl, has been taking care of herself for what seems forever. And because of that she's developed an incredibly fierce sense of independence. She rarely shows weakness. And if she feels weak, she gets over it in the very next breath. Simply put, <b>
  <u>I have a girl crush on her. </u>
</b><br /><br />With Ella's life's doing a 180--from pauper to princess--she's thrust into the Royal Mansion. That could easily change her as a person, yet it doesn't. Ella Harper is a good to her core. But while she's good, she's also strong. She takes no shit and gives zero fucks as well. <br /><br /><i>[.... "I lift a finger and trail it slowly across his naked pecs, my nail scraping across his smooth skin. His breath hitches, almost imperceptibly, but it’s there.<br />My heart leaps to my throat and blood begins to pound in places that I absolutely do not want to be associated with Reed Royal.<br />"You’re playing a dangerous game,” he rasps out.<br />Don’t I know it. Still, I can’t let Reed see he’s gotten to me. I pull my hand away, folding the fingers into a fist. “I don’t know any other way to play it.” ....]</i><br /><br />All the Royal boys have distinct personalities. From Easton, to Gideon, to Sawyer, to Sebastian, they're all intriguing in their own way. But our hero is Reed Royal. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>REED MOTHER FUCKING ROYAL! Prince of aloof fuckery!</u>
</b><br /><br />Reed is the ringleader of the bunch. When he says jump, they say "YES, SIR!" He sets the standard in the Royal house and at Astor Park Prep, their High School! He's cold and his heart seems impossible to penetrate. I have so many thoughts on this man! I've analyzed him over and over and over again. I could say so much, but I don't want to spoil. So, I'm not going to. But I'll say this... I think our Hero has a soft heart. I think he's deliciously sexy. He makes me feel like a cougar. <i>
  <b>RAWR!</b>
</i> I definitely think I'm in love him. And I think things are going to get very juicy, and maybe even a touch scandalous, in book 2. **waggles brows**<br /><br /><i>[.... "The apple is dangling in front of me, juicy red and delicious, but, like the fairy tale, Reed Royal is the villain disguised as a pretty prince. Taking a bit out of him would be a huge mistake." ....]</i><br /><br />Also, I need to mention! I'm always skeptical when two authors I love write together. Especially when those authors have two very distinct writing voices. I mean, it's ELLE KENNEDY and JEN FREDERICK! Hello, major awesomeness. But with them writing under Erin Watt, I couldn't tell who wrote what!!! It was perfect, seamless, fluid. Effortless writing and transitions that I just devoured. I am so ready to read <b>EVERYTHING</b> these two collaborate on.<br /><br />Another thing... <br /><br />You've probably heard this already but <i>Paper Princess</i> definitely had a TV show feel. I could absolutely see this on the <i>CW</i> or one of those TV networks that everyone loves. I'm not a huge movie person. I've never watched <i>Cruel Intentions</i> (don't judge). And I've only seen an episode or two of <i>Gossip girl</i> (I'm lame, I know). But I could absolutely imagine this as something even I, a non TV watcher, would invest in. I would definitely be there every week, snacks at the ready, bells on, waiting for my weekly fix of the <b>Royal TV show.</b><br /><br />Overall, I loved it. From the first words to the last, I was <b>BEYOND</b> hooked. This is chock full of drama, sex, dysfunction, but also heart. The writing is good. The characters are enthralling. And the plot line is juicy. With plenty of twists and turns to keep you on your toes, it's an intoxicating read. It is the first in the series. However, I urge you to try it out. You'll <b>LOVE</b> it. I'm sure of it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9283827440089656331" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1580876035?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2016-ya-challenge">2016-ya-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1580876035" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14345310987639634287"><b>5 stars</b> <br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%208/99165519-BE7C-45D1-80B9-6458D2AD5408_zps67osmna5.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458896647i/18544935._SY540_.jpg' alt=' photo 99165519-BE7C-45D1-80B9-6458D2AD5408_zps67osmna5.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I honestly can’t tell you the last time I’ve read a book that was this addictive. This book was like crack to me. I started it on a day when I had things going on and no matter what I had to do, I was itching to read it. I was sneaking in chapters. I devoured this book. It was angsty in the best way possible, had a strong heroine and a family of brothers who ended up being the most lovable jerks- but trust me, you won’t love them all the time! <br/><br/>Ella Harper is tough. She’s only 17, but</span>
  <span id="freeText14345310987639634287" style="display:none"><b>5 stars</b> <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%208/99165519-BE7C-45D1-80B9-6458D2AD5408_zps67osmna5.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458896647i/18544935._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 99165519-BE7C-45D1-80B9-6458D2AD5408_zps67osmna5.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I honestly can’t tell you the last time I’ve read a book that was this addictive. This book was like crack to me. I started it on a day when I had things going on and no matter what I had to do, I was itching to read it. I was sneaking in chapters. I devoured this book. It was angsty in the best way possible, had a strong heroine and a family of brothers who ended up being the most lovable jerks- but trust me, you won’t love them all the time! <br><br>Ella Harper is tough. She’s only 17, but ever since her mom died of cancer, she’s been making it on her own. It’s been a struggle, but she does it. Out of no where, a man she’s never met, Callum Royal, claims to be her legal guardian and takes her home with him. And his 5 sons await. <br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“You should know whatever game you're playing, you can't win. Not against all of us.If you leave now, you won't be hurt. If you stay, we'll break you so bad that you'll be crawling away.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i> Yeah, these Royal boys can be brutal. Especially the leader of their pack, Reed. I loved how Ella handled them. She is so bad ass. She always stays true to herself and says what is on her mind. She’ll play their game if she has too… These boys think they know her. They have no idea. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%208/A3D1C67D-0D66-447B-B9B3-D66E5FF3257A_zpsclzwwjcl.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458896647i/18544936._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo A3D1C67D-0D66-447B-B9B3-D66E5FF3257A_zpsclzwwjcl.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The sexual tension between Reed and Ella is off the charts. Although neither one likes the other, sometimes it seems like Reed straight up despises Ella, you can feel the heat between them. The authors did a fantastic job writing these characters. I never hated these Royal boys so much that I felt they were completely unredeemable. Of course, Reed was great (some of the time) but one of my favorite characters in the book was Easton Royal. He was so funny and became a friend to Ella when she needed one. <br><br>After spending more time with these Royal boys, Ella sees who they really are and why they do the things they do. She’s resilient. She doesn’t back down and she doesn't give up. On them, or herself.<br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%208/C88DAA56-9B32-4270-90B2-744A9793FEE7_zpstn6zrwvb.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458896647i/18544937._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo C88DAA56-9B32-4270-90B2-744A9793FEE7_zpstn6zrwvb.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I thought the authors did a fantastic job of co-writing this story. It was so smooth and had such a great flow, I couldn’t tell who had written what. <br><br>This book completely <b>stressed me out</b>. There were twists, turns, angst, drama, revenge, betrayal, love, friendship and more than one jaw dropping moment. That ending. I can’t even with that. WHAT WAS THAT??? I was dying. Let me tell you now, when the second book releases in a few short months, I will have no problem recalling what happened at the end. My jaw is still on the floor and my heart still hurts from reading that last chapter! <br><br>If you’re looking for an all-consuming story that’s full of angst- and as the authors describe it ‘a love child of Cruel Intentions and Gossip Girl’ &lt;—- very accurate IMO- READ THIS BOOK!!!!!! I couldn’t get enough! <br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“No one wants to be ruined. We all want to be saved.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%208/FFECAC92-229C-4DB2-B03A-62D952852884_zpsi7xhjrwq.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458896647i/18544938._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo FFECAC92-229C-4DB2-B03A-62D952852884_zpsi7xhjrwq.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_1609364308" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1609364308" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1609364308?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1609364308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5896220065454487209">I have to admit, I didn't expect to like this book, but it has a <i>Hana Yori Dango</i> (Meteor Garden, Boys Over Flowers, whatever you call it) sort of vibe.<blockquote>
  <i>"...all it takes is one word from him and you’ll be nothing here. Insignificant. Invisible. Or worse.”</i>
</blockquote>This is no brilliant work of literature, believe me, but what it was is <b>utterly entertaining</b>. The reason I compare it to <i>Hana Yori Dango</i> (HYD) is the premise. It's a bit different, but the similarity is still there. <br/><br/>Ella Harper is plucked from</span>
  <span id="freeText5896220065454487209" style="display:none">I have to admit, I didn't expect to like this book, but it has a <i>Hana Yori Dango</i> (Meteor Garden, Boys Over Flowers, whatever you call it) sort of vibe.<blockquote>
  <i>"...all it takes is one word from him and you’ll be nothing here. Insignificant. Invisible. Or worse.”</i>
</blockquote>This is no brilliant work of literature, believe me, but what it was is <b>utterly entertaining</b>. The reason I compare it to <i>Hana Yori Dango</i> (HYD) is the premise. It's a bit different, but the similarity is still there. <br /><br />Ella Harper is plucked from poverty and a hard life to live with her "guardian," a wealthy man with five sons. She is smart, strong, a survivor, and is plopped into a chi-chi world and ultra-rich school where four of the sons attend, all of whom are determined to make her life a living hell.<br /><br />The school she attends is straight out of HYD.<blockquote>
  <i>“Astor Park is a prep school with a P.” Savannah keeps walking. There’s no quit button on her. “Every family in the state wants their kids to go here, but it’s exclusive. You can’t just have money to get in. Everyone that attends, even the scholarship students, are here because they have something special to offer."</i>
</blockquote>I don't like New Adult, I can tell you that, but this book was surprisingly fun. It always takes a lot for me to overcome my prejudice of the genre, and what surprised me about this book was the fact that there are other female characters in the book.<br /><br />The difference between this book and HYD is that all the guys are asshats. If you're expecting a bunch of flowery boys, you're gonna be disappointed because all of them are alpha male assholes of the Jericho-fucking-Barrons sort. I hated their asses, and to be honest, I still sort of do. Violence and intimidation is never something I approve of, but at least this book doesn't try to make excuses to portray these boys as anything but major douchebags. There's no quiet, sweet moment with violin-playing Hanazawa Rui here. This being NA, of course there is redemption, and it's realistic enough to be believable.<br /><br />The star of the story, Ella, was surprisingly likeable. She's strong, but not over the top. She yearns for love and acceptance, hiding it behind a hard exterior, and her character was well-developed throughout the story. <br /><br />Again, don't get me wrong, this isn't the next great American novel, but it's a soap opera and it's damned entertaining.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5896220065454487209" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1618548094?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink">Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1618548094" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5878065717085178965">DNF at 70% - Clearly I need to research books a little more before I read them.<br/><br/>This was just... wow. First off, I didn't realize this was NA, but thats fine. I don't mind NA if things are tastefully and respectfully done. Most NA books I've read glorify some pretty disgusting relationship issues. Whatever. I couldn't sleep so I just kept reading- waiting for some redeeming factor. <br/><br/>So Ella, the protagonist has had a seriously rough life. She lost her mom, never had a dad, and had to come close to</span>
  <span id="freeText5878065717085178965" style="display:none">DNF at 70% - Clearly I need to research books a little more before I read them.<br /><br />This was just... wow. First off, I didn't realize this was NA, but thats fine. I don't mind NA if things are tastefully and respectfully done. Most NA books I've read glorify some pretty disgusting relationship issues. Whatever. I couldn't sleep so I just kept reading- waiting for some redeeming factor. <br /><br />So Ella, the protagonist has had a seriously rough life. She lost her mom, never had a dad, and had to come close to selling herself just to make ends meet. When her mom was alive, she was a stripper and had several boyfriends that sexually abused Ella. That is what we're told anyway- but Ella doesn't seem to suffer any mental challenges despite her past. Nope, she easily adjusts to life with the "Royals" and constantly talks about how horny she is despite her past, her abuse, and the way they treat her. <br /><br />Come. On. <br /><br />For a girl that has had that much of a physical tole - I find it this very hard to believe.<br /><br />I don't know if the author has ever met anyone who has lived a life of constant trauma (I've been through quite a bit myself)... but I'm very unconvinced in her attempts to write Ella's character. Not to mention her past in terms of her body- well this topic should be handled with care and tact. I feel like the author has never had to write about real mental struggles/pain ESPECIALLY relating to poverty or sexual abuse. <br /><br />Those issues aside...<br /><br />If you want to read a very predictable/typical NA book where a girl is thrown into a rich fancy life and is constantly gaping after the "bad boy" and has to face your very common "bitch who runs the school" then this book is for you, granted you want to read about dangly parts. Listen, I'm not judging, just forewarning.<br /><br />Seriously, I don't mind skipping a few pages in a story that are TMI for me- if the story is strong enough. But this? Read the spoiler at your own risk... <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Ella comes from a bad past. Ella all the sudden is rich and has to live with 5 boys who are "hot." The "meanest &amp; most disturbed" one is the one she lusts after. Of course, he lusts after her too. Of course they "hate" each other. Of course, she goes to a party and another guy tries to take advantage of her and "mean hot boy" comes to her rescue." Then, because she got "drugged" at said party, she wants "release" and "mean hot boy" and her screw around despite the fact that she's drugged out of her mind. Thats where I quit. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Guys, I promise you can find plenty of books with a similar plot line that are much better written.<br /><br />Anyway, thats about all I have to say. <br /><br /><a href="http://www.herbookishthings.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> ~ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/herbookishthings/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ~ <a href="https://twitter.com/herbookishthing" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ~ <a href="https://www.etsy.com/shop/herbookishthings" rel="nofollow noopener">Etsy</a></span>

<div id="review_1593065086" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1593065086" />
    <a title="Candace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16384209-candace"><img alt="Candace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459720769p2/16384209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1593065086?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=hate-that-i-love-them">hate-that-i-love-them</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=childhood-loves">childhood-loves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=forbidden-romance">forbidden-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=shocking-twists">shocking-twists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=rich-guys">rich-guys</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1593065086" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1048818885506289419">I had been seeing reviews for this series pop up all over my friends' pages. Knowing that I wanted to read this series and find out what all the fuss was about, I told myself I'd wait for the Audible version to be released. So I waited...and waited...and waited some more. When I started to see the glowing reviews for the third, and final, book in the series, and still there was no sign of an audiobook release, I knew I had to start this series. So, I downloaded the Kindle edition of 'Paper Princ</span>
  <span id="freeText1048818885506289419" style="display:none">I had been seeing reviews for this series pop up all over my friends' pages. Knowing that I wanted to read this series and find out what all the fuss was about, I told myself I'd wait for the Audible version to be released. So I waited...and waited...and waited some more. When I started to see the glowing reviews for the third, and final, book in the series, and still there was no sign of an audiobook release, I knew I had to start this series. So, I downloaded the Kindle edition of 'Paper Princess' and never looked back.<br /><br />Several days later, I've finished all three books and am suffering from a significant book hangover. Let me tell you, this series is addicting! From the moment I began reading 'Paper Princess', I was consumed with this story. <br /><br />Every day is a struggle for Ella Harper. The daughter of a single mother, she has spent her childhood running from town to town as her mother jumps from one bad relationship to another. Although her upbringing was anything but stable, she always knew she had the love of her mother.<br /><br />However, when Ella's mother grows ill with cancer, Ella is forced to assume adult responsibilities as a young teenager. When her mother dies, Ella is left all alone. She does what she has to do to survive and stay out of the foster care system.<br /><br />By the time Ella is seventeen, she has registered herself in high school by forging her mother's signature. She is working three jobs and living in a rundown apartment. She'd kill to have the superficial "problems" that her classmates face. <br /><br />Just when she doesn't think her situation could get any worse, she is reduced to accepting a job dancing nude. She'd danced before, but never fully nude. Clinging to that tiny bit of modesty meant a lot to Ella, but she had to sacrifice it to survive.<br /><br />Then, a man she'd never heard of before shows up and insists that he is her legal guardian. It is evident that Callum Royal is wealthy, but Ella has no intention of leaving with the man who claims to be the best friend of her recently deceased father. She never had any relationship with the sperm donor that gifted her life and then promptly left her mother in the dust, much less the stranger that claims to have custody of her.<br /><br />Despite her best efforts to evade him, Callum persists until he has Ella on a jet and headed to his home. When they arrive at the mansion that is to be her new home, Ella is immediately made aware of the fact that she isn't the only one that doesn't want her there. In spite of Callum's best efforts to make Ella feel welcomed, his five teenage sons make their distaste for Ella equally clear.<br /><br />Reed, the second oldest son, but the oldest son still living at home, is clearly calling the shots. His younger brothers follow his lead and Ella finds herself fighting a losing battle against all of the Royal boys. They're sure that she's out for their father's money, among other things, and they're determined to make her life a living hell.<br /><br />And so, Ella's rags to riches journey begins...<br /><br />She is submersed in a world of luxury and excess that she'd never imagined existed in real life. Enrolled in the same elite prep school as the Royal boys, she is constantly reminded that she doesn't belong. Reed rules the school, just as he rules the Royal house. As she struggles to adjust to her new life and blend in, Reed is equally determined to push her out. <br /><br />The bullying and cruelty that ensues was incredibly sad. I have to admit that I geared up several times as I read some of the things that poor Ella went through. Yet, despite everything she persevered.<br /><br />Somewhere along the way, Reed gives up on his mission to terrorize Ella. The attraction between them keeps coming to the surface and they eventually make nice. Of course, once Reed decides to give Ella a shot, his brother's follow suit. From that point forward, it is like somebody flipped a switch. Ella and Reed go from being enemies to being head-over-heels. It happened quick enough to leave my head spinning.<br /><br />Despite my reservations, mainly that Reed never had to "pay" for his maltreatment of Ella, I still found myself completely addicted to this story. In so many ways, this story is reminiscent of another one of my favorite high school sagas, 'Fallen Crest High'. The over-the-top lives of privilege and excess lived by these kids is unreal. <br /><br />This story has definitely become a guilty pleasure of mine. Like so many of my friends, I am hooked! As expected, this first book ended with a huge cliffhanger. I started reading the second book immediately. You'll want to do the same, so have 'Broken Prince' ready to go when you finish 'Paper Princess'. Loved it!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1048818885506289419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8568617210694585168"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464344588i/19228937.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464344588ra/19228938.gif' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464344588ra/19228939.gif' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>★★★★★! Paper Princess, book 1 of 3. Modern tale rags to riches Cinderella in high school setting with six potential suitors & all the elements of a fairytale!</b><br/><br/><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“You may have lost your family, but you’re not alone anymore, Ella. You’re a Royal now.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br/><u>Books in The Royals series should be read in order:</u><br/><b>Book 1: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1602099452' rel='nofollow noopener'>Paper Princess</a><br/>Book 2: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1610986929' rel='nofollow noopener'>Broken Prince</a><br/>Book 3: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1610987129' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twisted Palace</a></b><br/><br/><b>Paper Princess</b> (book 1) is the riveting opening to a glued to-your-kindle saga. <br/><br/><b>
  <i>One woman, six men, money, gree</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText8568617210694585168" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464344588i/19228937.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464344588ra/19228938.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464344588ra/19228939.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>★★★★★! Paper Princess, book 1 of 3. Modern tale rags to riches Cinderella in high school setting with six potential suitors &amp; all the elements of a fairytale!</b><br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“You may have lost your family, but you’re not alone anymore, Ella. You’re a Royal now.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br><u>Books in The Royals series should be read in order:</u><br><b>Book 1: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1602099452" rel="nofollow noopener">Paper Princess</a><br>Book 2: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1610986929" rel="nofollow noopener">Broken Prince</a><br>Book 3: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1610987129" rel="nofollow noopener">Twisted Palace</a></b><br><br><b>Paper Princess</b> (book 1) is the riveting opening to a glued to-your-kindle saga. <br><br><b>
  <i>One woman, six men, money, greed, excess, sex deceit, betrayal, secrets.</i>
</b><br><br>Forced into stripping to pay her mother’s medical bills <b>Ella Harper</b> has tried to fly under the radar until she can turn eighteen and not risk ending up in the foster care system. But one day her meager and humble strip club is graced with the visit by a too-handsome-for-his-own-good billionaire father of five, <b>Callum Royal</b> who claims to be her father’s friend and her guardian.<br><br><b>
  <i>In an instance her life goes from rags to riches.</i>
</b><br><br>Settled into the Royals’ castle high upon the hill she is faced with five handsome princes, <b>Gideon, Reed, Easton, Sawyer and Sebastian</b> none too happy to see her. The story goes on to follow them at school, home and the party scene, as Ella gets to know a little bit about each brother. Unlikely friendships are formed, lines drawn, truces forged and suitor aligning themselves with each prince having a stake.<br><br><b>
  <i>It’s a modern day fairy tale that will leave you pining not for one, not even five, but six to-die-for heroes!</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464344588ra/19228940.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Seven words to describe <b>Ella Harper:</b> Strong, independent, loyal, private, charismatic, reflective, naïve and unforgettable.<br><br><b>Paper Princess,</b> brilliantly told from Ella’s POV, spellbound me all the way to its shocking and oh so perfect ending. I am considering hibernation until book 2, <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1610986929" rel="nofollow noopener">Broken Prince.</a>
</b><br><br><a>
  <blockquote>
    <i>
      <b>“You want this?” He pumps himself slowly. “You can have it. Lick it, suck it, fuck it, anything you want, baby. As long it’s just with me.”</b>
    </i>
  </blockquote>
</a><br>***<br>Ella’s rating: 5 stars<br>Callum’s rating: 5 stars <br>Reed’s rating: 5 stars <br>Gideon’s rating: 4.5 stars <br>Easton’s rating: 4 stars <br>Sexual tension rating: 5 stars<br>Sex scenes rating: 4 stars<br>Sex scenes frequency: 4 stars<br>Plot rating: 5 stars<br>Dialogue rating: 5 stars<br>Storytelling rating: 5 stars<br>Story ending rating: N/A<br>**********************************************<br><b>Overall rating: 5 stars<br><br>Would I recommend this series: Yes.<br>Would I re-read this series: Yes.<br>Would I read future books by this author: Yes.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464345141ra/19229027.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

</i><br><br>OH MYYYY GOOOOD! I wish you guys could hear me literally scream at this book.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1500637574ra/23368555.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>This whole book was a huge WTF moment. <br><br>Why is this thing even allowed to exist?!!!! <br><br>I have never been this pissed at a book before. It was wrong on so many levels, I don't even know where to start. <br><br>Could you just puh-lease stop romanticising bloody abusive relationships, FOR THE LOVE OF GOD! <br><br>Can you imagine all the teenage girls reading this book and thinking that freaking assholes are hot because this idiot character Ella is attracted to jerks?????<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1500600314ra/23363286.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>This book is the most disgusting thing I have read in my <b>life.</b> All you can find in here is abuse, near-rape and a creepy characters. <br><br>If any teenage girl is reading this review, I need you to understand that abusive relationships are not okay. If someone is being a jerk to you it is NOT okay. If someone calls you a slut, you get out of there now! If you've been drudged and nearly raped, you need to talk to someone. <br><br>*sighs deeply* what has the world come to? <br><br>The fact that they kept referring to Ella as their sister makes it TEN TIMES more disgusting and creepy. And don't even get me started on the dad. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1443640727ra/16388236.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><i>
  <blockquote>“What do you want?”<br>“To talk.”<br>“Then talk here.”<br>“Get in here, Ella.”<br>“No.”<br>“Yes.”<br>I drop my arms and walk into the cabin. Something about this guy…he issues a command and I obey.</blockquote>
</i> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499764761ra/23264368.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><i>
  <blockquote>He’s a jerk and he wants to hurt you, I scream at my body. My nipples pucker despite my warning.</blockquote>
</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1500638993ra/23368766.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I don't recommend this book to anyone and I have no interest whatsoever to read the rest of this series. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381956919ra/5473696.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>Pre-reading</b><br>Most of my friends absolutely hated this book. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440877824ra/16036030.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="8146845605467273285" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1611416490" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1611416490" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1611416490?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Katerina by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/37314676-nicoleta-e-addicted-to-books">NiCoLeTa E. {Addicted To Books}</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1611416490" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16816281282535722351">You're kidding me.<br/><i>You're kidding me.</i><br/><b>
  <i>You're fucking kidding me!!</i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467803142ra/19631456.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“These Royals will ruin you”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><i>I</i> am the one ruined beyond repair. I am <b>livid</b>. You can practically see smoke steaming from my ears and pieces of my heart falling to the floor.<br/><i><b>I</b> have fallen apart.</i><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467803442ra/19631550.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You should know whatever game you're playing, you can't win. Not against all of us. If you leave now, you won't be hurt. If you stay, we'll break you so bad that you'll be crawling away.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>I beg you to forgive me for no</span>
  <span id="freeText16816281282535722351" style="display:none">You're kidding me.<br><i>You're kidding me.</i><br><b>
  <i>You're fucking kidding me!!</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467803142ra/19631456.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“These Royals will ruin you”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><i>I</i> am the one ruined beyond repair. I am <b>livid</b>. You can practically see smoke steaming from my ears and pieces of my heart falling to the floor.<br><i><b>I</b> have fallen apart.</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467803442ra/19631550.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You should know whatever game you're playing, you can't win. Not against all of us. If you leave now, you won't be hurt. If you stay, we'll break you so bad that you'll be crawling away.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I beg you to forgive me for not writing a proper review, it seems that my thoughts and emotions are really tangled. Frankly, a part of me wonders why I liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28678119.Paper_Princess__The_Royals___1_" title="Paper Princess (The Royals, #1) by Erin Watt" rel="nofollow noopener">Paper Princess</a>. Every single character was <b>broken</b>, every relationship <b>twisted</b> and <b>dysfunctional</b>, and I couldn't help but cringe at some scenes. I couldn't relate with Ella nor understand her actions, I hated the boys at first and at the end all I could do was yell at a certain someone who did a certain something and damaged my faith in him.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467803880ra/19631609.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>But <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28678119.Paper_Princess__The_Royals___1_" title="Paper Princess (The Royals, #1) by Erin Watt" rel="nofollow noopener">Paper Princess</a> was <b>addictive</b>.<br>It's definitely one of the books I'd call <b>guilty pleasures</b>, there were so many things <b>wrong</b> with the characters and their decisions and their life styles I can't even begin to describe, but they grew on me despite my will. And I am pretty certain that 17 year olds <i>don't</i> act this way. When <i>I</i> was seventeen, me and my classmates used to pretend we'd film a movie, Indiana Jones style, with me as an archaeologist searching for the secrets of the sanctuary of Deplhi and everyone had a ridiculous part, like my Chinese sidekick or the "random stranger that passed by and said hi". My point is, we were a bit childish. We didn't drug other people or obey the rich kids at school. We were normal. And nothing about the Royals was normal.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I'm not mad at you. I'm mad at myself. I did this. Well, Easton and I. I brought this on you. I'm Reed the Destroyer.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Like I said before, I hated the Royal boys at first. They were dirty and horny and mean. But eventually, when I understood their behavior and how hurt they were, I felt a pang of sympathy. Nothing justifies making another person's life miserable, but not everyone deals with their grief and resentment in socially acceptable ways. While I hated Easton, he suddenly became my precious cinnamon roll. And Reed, well, what can I say about him?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414082919ra/11606087.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The rich, fucked up asshole. The Destroyer. </b> There wasn't a chance I wouldn't fall for him, God knows how easily attracted I am to characters beautiful and broken. His <b>chemistry</b> with Ella was a being of its own, I could feel the flames licking my body and I sweat under their meaningful looks and <b>scorching scenes</b>. <b>Angst and tension</b> at their finest, ladies and gentlemen!<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Look, I like you. Didn’t think I would but I do, and because I like you, I feel the need to warn you that we Royals are pretty fucked up. We’re good in bed, but out of it? We’re like a stage four hurricane.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I don't know how I feel about Ella. She was <b>ballsy</b> and I liked it, but she tended to be provocative without reason. I don't judge her for her profession, she did everything she could to survive and that was admirable. I do blame her mother though. Yes I understand that given the circumstances she did the only thing she knew, but when you have a young daughter you don't change boyfriends that often and move across the country every time you fall in love! That's just selfish!<br><br>After <i>that</i> ending, I'm starving for the next book like a junkie craving her dose. <b>Paper Princess found its way to my heart and now owns it. </b>Oh, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14902188.Erin_Watt" title="Erin Watt" rel="nofollow noopener">Erin Watt</a>, <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467805987ra/19632007.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="16816281282535722351" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1580493882" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1580493882" />
    <a title="Lana ❇✾DG Romance❇✾" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5498948-lana-dg-romance"><img alt="Lana ❇✾DG Romance❇✾" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1376622739p2/5498948.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1580493882?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lana ❇✾DG Romance❇✾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lana ❇✾DG Romance❇✾" href="/user/show/5498948-lana-dg-romance">Lana ❇✾DG Romance❇✾</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5498948-lana-dg-romance?shelf=best-of-the-best">best-of-the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5498948-lana-dg-romance?shelf=favorite-heroine">favorite-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5498948-lana-dg-romance?shelf=highschool">highschool</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5498948-lana-dg-romance?shelf=famous-hero">famous-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5498948-lana-dg-romance?shelf=favorite-alpha-hero">favorite-alpha-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5498948-lana-dg-romance?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5498948-lana-dg-romance?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1580493882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10456416874958718041"><b>5 Stars</b><br/><img src='https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458450109r/18489702.jpg?v=1458450112858' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png' width='50' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>You should know whatever game you're playing, you can't win. Not against all of us.<br/>If you leave now, you won't be hurt. If you stay, we'll break you so bad that you'll be crawling away."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1458529596ra/18497867.gif' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Let's talk about things that trigger my one-clicker for a second here, shall we?<br/><br/><b>Authors:</b> we have a book that's basically an angst filled love child of <i>Cruel Intentions</i> and <i>Gossip Girl</i>. There's YA kind angst but with NA kind scenarios. There's hate lust, an incredible tough as nails heroine, a b</span>
  <span id="freeText10456416874958718041" style="display:none"><b>5 Stars</b><br><img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458450109r/18489702.jpg?v=1458450112858" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">You should know whatever game you're playing, you can't win. Not against all of us.<br>If you leave now, you won't be hurt. If you stay, we'll break you so bad that you'll be crawling away."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1458529596ra/18497867.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Let's talk about things that trigger my one-clicker for a second here, shall we?<br><br><b>Authors:</b> we have a book that's basically an angst filled love child of <i>Cruel Intentions</i> and <i>Gossip Girl</i>. There's YA kind angst but with NA kind scenarios. There's hate lust, an incredible tough as nails heroine, a bunch of sexy rich and entitled brothers that have enough issues to fill up Grand Canyon, a broody as hell alphahole hero that you'll love to hate but secretly mainly love, and all of it is wrapped up in a story that's more addicting than crack.<br><br><b>Me:</b> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1458529596ra/18497868.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That about sum it up for you then? Good. Because if ever there was ever a book that was custom written for me, this is that book. At first the YA tag turned me away because I'm not a reader that enjoys YA. But the only thing YA about this book are the characters' ages; the heroine is 17 and the setting is in high school. However, the events that take place are focused towards a more mature NA, which just happens to be my catnip.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">Some kids dream of traveling the world, owning fast cars, big houses. Me? I want my own apartment, a fridge full of food, and a steady paying job, preferably one that's as exciting as paste drying.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Ella Harper is exactly the kind of heroine I love to read about. She's led a hard life in her young 17 years. Her mom may have been flighty and jumping from one boyfriend to the next all her life while struggling to support the both of them, but she's all she's ever known. Now that her mother has passed away, Ella has nothing and no one and struggles to make ends meet just to make it through high school so she can go on to college. When a man shows up at her school claiming to be her legal guardian and her father's best friend, she's rightful skeptical. But Callum is determined to help once he sees the way Ella's been living and it's not long before she arrives on the Royal doorstep much to the disgruntlement of Callum's five sons.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">The Royal boys are not what I expected. They don't look like rich pricks in preppy clothes. They look like terrifying thugs who can snap me like a twig. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>To say they're not happy to see her, is an understatement. The Royals rule the school Ella now goes to and what they say goes. They're determined not to go easy on the new girl, especially one that clearly doesn't belong in their world. But Ella is no wilting wallflower. This girl gives as good as she gets and boy does that make for some entertaining reading.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">This will never be my home. I don't belong in splendor, I belong in squalor. That's what I know. It's what I'm comfortable with because squalor doesn't lie to you. It's not wrapped up in a pretty package. It is what it is.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This book was the perfect combination of angst with a slow burn of hate/lust all wrapped around an undercurrent of a slow burn sexual tension. Reed Royal is a character that you can't help but love even while you love to hate him. He's not nice to Ella, not at all, but yet the way that he's written you can't help but know there's something beneath the surface of what he lets you see.; something dark and deep and you're just itching to scratch at it to know what it is.<br><img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458531328r/18497928.jpg?v=1458531331201" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380397315i/766520.png" width="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg">Here's the deal," he says. "My brother and father are off-limits to you. If you have an itch, you come to me. I'll take care of it. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I absolutely devoured this book, and by devoured I mean I couldn't put it down for even a second. It's been a long while where a book has managed to suck me in as much as this one did. It's filled with teenage angst and drama and characters that you can't help but fall for. The authors did a phenomenal job creating these characters that are so real they practically jump off at the pages. I was enamored with the story. I was hooked on each page like a junky craving their next fix and angst just happens to be my drug of choice. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1458531509ra/18497954.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As for that ending? Well let's just say I may or may not be rocking myself in a corner as we speak while I wait for July 25 to finally get here<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1458531509ra/18497955.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>ARC courtesy of author in exchange for an honest review</i><br><br><b>Find me on:<br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/DirtyGirlRomance?" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436986543i/15525717.png" width="40" height="40" alt="Follow me on facebook" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> <a href="https://twitter.com/DirtyGrlRomance" target="twitter" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436986543i/15525718.png" width="40" height="40" alt="Follow Me on Twitter" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> <a href="http://www.dirtygirlromance.com" target="blog" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436986543i/15525719.png" width="40" height="40" alt="blog" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><a href="http://dirtygirlromance.com" target="blog" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436477285i/15465455._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10456416874958718041" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

This book deserves its own category in my GR bookshelves, really, I was tempted to make a new shelf called: "WTF" just to put this book in (still tempted, so maybe I'll end up doing it). I mean, this book was ridiculous. The amount of drama was astounding.   <span id="freeText12716261186999944569" style="display:none">Not sure if 2.5 or 3 stars? This book deserves its own category in my GR bookshelves, really, I was tempted to make a new shelf called: "WTF" just to put this book in (still tempted, so maybe I'll end up doing it). I mean, this book was ridiculous. The amount of drama was astounding. I was rolling my eyes ALL THE TIME and not only because of the drama, but also because everything that happened was (I repeat) ridiculous! I think I said "wtf" out loud more than 50 times while reading this.<br /><br />Nevertheless, it was a fast read and an addictive one, so I might give the second book a try. Because of that and also because this one ended on a massive cliffhanger and I have to admit I'm curious about what will happen.</span>

    <a title="V.   <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">NA readers menage readers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors?shelf=cliffhanger">cliffhanger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors?shelf=slutshaming">slutshaming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors?shelf=ow">ow</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31006810-v-a-court-of-wings-and-ruin-is-new-adult-erotica-but-goodreads-editors?shelf=na-pretending-to-be-ya">na-pretending-to-be-ya</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1610640521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16616567138451597856">TRIGGER FOR DATE RAPE VICTIMS<br/>I hate when this happens. When everyone loves a book that I don't. I hate being minority. I signed up to goodreads to fangirl over books with other people, to like the five star reviews and ignore the haters. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460676914ra/18773535.gif' width='300' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I love when all my friends read the same book and love it as much as I did.<br/><br/> I hate to rate this book. A lot of my goodreads friends have LOVED IT! And I can see why. For the most part of the book I loved it, too. Then the twist happens and everyone still loves t</span>
  <span id="freeText16616567138451597856" style="display:none">TRIGGER FOR DATE RAPE VICTIMS<br>I hate when this happens. When everyone loves a book that I don't. I hate being minority. I signed up to goodreads to fangirl over books with other people, to like the five star reviews and ignore the haters. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460676914ra/18773535.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I love when all my friends read the same book and love it as much as I did.<br><br> I hate to rate this book. A lot of my goodreads friends have LOVED IT! And I can see why. For the most part of the book I loved it, too. Then the twist happens and everyone still loves the book, but I don't. I'm left outside. So, yeah it sucks to be minority.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460676914ra/18773536.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I hate giving bad ratings. I'd rather not finish a book than give a bad rating. However if in other occassions I prefer not to post a review or even a rating because <br>a) I don't want to waste more time than the book deserves<br>or<br><br>b)I can't pinpoint what I didn't like,<br><br>In this case I think I have to warn other readers who might have the same problem than I have. If you are warned, you might enjoy the book more than I did. In addition, I can tell when the book was ruined FOR ME. If you are warned of what you will find you might even give a 5 star rating, that I think the authors deserve because for the most part their book is not bad.<br><br><br>I think everyone will love this book way more than I do. People should give it a try. The authors have a way with words and for the majority of the book I THOUGHT THIS WAS FANTASTICLY compelling and AWESOME, I never considered not finishing it because the emotions, the characters, the journey were so good that I just couldn't put the book down. I would recommend this book to anyone who isn't a freak like me: A freak who has a high sensibility on <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[CHEATING. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460677861ra/18773589.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Why? Oh Why? Can't authors think of another way to create drama? Everything was going so well, then that twist. IIt ruins the sequels for me. I asked a refund from amazon and I'm not continuing with the series. Again that's me. I'm extremely sensitive to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[cheating. When I read a romance I want to root for the couple and I don't want the hero to have eyes for anyone but the heroine. I'm the kind of freak that thinks of Travis Maddox as a cheater and same from Kayden from the Coincidence of Callie and Kayden and Drew evans from Tangled . Yes those guys weren't with the heroines when they tried to/or slept with someone else, but once the hero has kissed the heroine EVERY INTERACTION WITH ANOTHER WOMAN even a kiss is for me a form of cheating. In this case Reed goes way beyond what Travis, Kayden and Drew did. It makes him undreedemable for me.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>I wish there had been a warning for that twist. I hate hate hate hate when the authors <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ make heroes cheat  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>This is also a NA book marketed as YA. I'm okay with sex scenes, actually I get bored if a NA book doesn't have at least a bit of sexual tension and I prefer self-published authors because they cross the YA/NA boundaries more often than traditional published books. I just think the ethical thing to do is to warn the readers that there's sex in the book so people who like sex will buy it, and people who prefer "clean" reads stay away. Readers under 18 should stay clear from this book as it contains <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ drugs and rape scenes.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>This book reminded me of Tijan's fallen crest series, except the twist I mentioned. I think that I wouldn't have hated the ending as much as I did if I haven't been so involved with Ella and Reed. If you don't mind <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[cheating heroes, if you don't mind cliffhangers (the sequel will come out soon)  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and you like Tiijan give this book a try. If you hate when NA is labeled as YA then this book might not be for you.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="16616567138451597856" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
